    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }

      AppleID.auth.init({

The highly-regarded but unpredictable ex-commando Pierre NiTmans is sent from Paris to the French Alps to investigate. Meanwhile, Karim Abdouf, a young Arab policeman, is trying to find out why the tomb of a young child has been desecrated. When a second body is found, high up in a glacier, the paths of the two policemen are joined in their search for the killers, a trail that embroils them with the mysterioius cult of the Crimson Rivers.</p></span>

    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1940326269" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16251780863214945839">One of the best thrillers I've ever read. Jean-Christophe Grang√©'s writing style is direct, full of force and embellished with beautiful, dark descriptions. In this book, the forces of nature, the darkness in the human mind and soul, and the mysticism associated with the Alps lead the two main characters down a spiral of lies and bloody deeds. <br/><br/>Karim and Pierre are realistic protagonists, their interactions are powerful, even entertaining at times. This is one of the rarest of cases where the fil</span>
  <span id="freeText16251780863214945839" style="display:none">One of the best thrillers I've ever read. Jean-Christophe Grang√©'s writing style is direct, full of force and embellished with beautiful, dark descriptions. In this book, the forces of nature, the darkness in the human mind and soul, and the mysticism associated with the Alps lead the two main characters down a spiral of lies and bloody deeds. <br /><br />Karim and Pierre are realistic protagonists, their interactions are powerful, even entertaining at times. This is one of the rarest of cases where the film is as good and satisfying as the book. Jean Reno and Vincent Cassel are marvellous.</span>
  <a data-text-id="16251780863214945839" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText1784251066189692615" style="display:none">Feverishly, Paul Bryant flicked through the pages on Manny's laptop. An icy sweat trickled down his forehead, mingling with the blood and dirt that was already encrusted into its luminous pallor. Now he understood Manny's secret. Everything made sense. He had been so--<br /><br />"Hold it right there."<br /><br />He looked up and froze. Manny stood facing him in the doorway, his right hand wrapped around the butt of a 7.65mm Glock. The barrel was pointing directly towards the Nottingham reviewer. <br /><br />"I see you've worked it out," laughed Manny grimly. "Though too late, I fear."<br /><br />"Of course," said Paul. "I was sure you were Not, but really you were her twin sister. That's why you kept posting things about Norwegian and quantum mechanics. It was staring me in the face all along."<br /><br />"Exactly," said Manny. Shadows danced in the corners of the cellar as he motioned with the torch he held in his other hand. "But now, I think you will be helping <i>me</i> write parodies... for some considerable time."<br /><br />A shot rang out. Manny slowly crumpled to the ground, a look of vast surprise on his face, as a woman entered the room.<br /><br />"How--" he murmured. <br /><br />"What you didn't know," said the newcomer, "was that Not was not just a twin, she was a triplet. I am Notte... which in Italian is 'night'. You see?"<br /><br />"Yes--" whispered Manny. A trickle of blood seeped from his mouth. "But I still don't understand one thing. Why am I reviewing <i>Les rivi√®res pourpres</i>?"<br /><br />A momentary look of annoyance contorted Notte's beautiful features. "I admit it, there are a few holes in the plot," she muttered. "Never mind, the screenwriter will fix that up in the movie. Or what do you say, Paul?"<br /><br />"Sounds good to me," agreed Bryant.<br /><br />They left together without a backward glance.</span>

<div id="review_1256238895" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1256238895" />
    <a title="Ari" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7792330-ari"><img alt="Ari" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1468152306p2/7792330.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1256238895?book_show_action=true">Apr 16, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ari" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ari" href="/user/show/7792330-ari">Ari</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780099449027" href="/book/show/2359329.Blood_Red_Rivers">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1256238895" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8051109059181973179">Although I enjoy thrillers, I don't usually read works written by men, and this book embodies pretty much everything I hate about the sub genre.<br/><br/>The murder in itself is gruesome, intricate, and frighteningly plausible, which is the reason why I decided to try and break my "no male authors" rule (also Jean Reno, but that's beside the point). But that's where my praise stops.<br/><br/>Ni√©mans is a boring male superintendent with and entire closet full of anger management issues, to the point where he's borde</span>
  <span id="freeText8051109059181973179" style="display:none">Although I enjoy thrillers, I don't usually read works written by men, and this book embodies pretty much everything I hate about the sub genre.<br /><br />The murder in itself is gruesome, intricate, and frighteningly plausible, which is the reason why I decided to try and break my "no male authors" rule (also Jean Reno, but that's beside the point). But that's where my praise stops.<br /><br />Ni√©mans is a boring male superintendent with and entire closet full of anger management issues, to the point where he's borderline psychopathic. And apparently I'm supposed to emphasise with this tortured, gruff man who barks orders and verbally abuses women (unless and even when he wants to fuck them - and apparently he wants to fuck literally every woman he comes in contact with) and more often than not physically abuses his male colleagues. Such a charming fellow. Even still, I would be more inclined to accept his violent inclination if he didn't act like an entitled, sleazy, sexist pig.<br /><br />Now, Abdouf is another can of worms entirely, and more to my liking. He's bright, bold, enthusiastic, better fleshed-out, and more importantly <i>different</i>. His own brand of manpain is easier to relate to - or ar the very least easier to indulge in. Even with all his faults Karim, as a character, is fundamentally likeable. His chapters read the fastest because I actually managed to switch my brain off and dive into the narration.<br /><br />As for the book as a whole, I guess a point could be made that no one is impervious to disease, be it physical or mental, and this novel sets out to explore all the different iterations of sickness - what it entails, the different faces it can assume, and so on - but in order to do that (blame it on the fact the book was written in 1997 or the distinctly French prose style) the greater message gets lost in a sea of manpain and lack of tangible conclusion that I absolutely don't care for.</span>
  <a data-text-id="8051109059181973179" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText10042044783246601884" style="display:none">For about the first half of the book I had to force myself to keep reading it. It did get a bit more interesting when it was becoming clear that the two cases were connected. But I didn't really get hooked.. The descriptions of what the protagonists saw were too long for my liking and contained a lot of strange phrases I'd never expect anyone to use in real life (they had me frowning at least once per chapter). Also the ending really disappointed me to be honest - it was way to abrupt and seemed a bit like the author was lacking ideas for a good ending and just tried to get it over with. <br />Sadly I have to say that this was one of the worst thrillers I've read so far - and I've read a lot.</span>

<div id="review_1610032492" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1610032492" />
    <a title="Vic Van" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/15874338-vic-van"><img alt="Vic Van" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1569926355p2/15874338.jpg" /></a>

  <span id="freeText2979577800819304022" style="display:none">For some time I have been searching for French crime writer who could live up to the standard, set by British novelist. Pierre Lema√Ætre was the first to match his English peers in my opinion. Jean-Christophe Grang√© is, most definitely, the second.<br /><br />The story is full of suspense from the very beginning until the very end. It is well-constructed. Each chapter ends with a real cliffhanger, which makes you want to read on and on. The setting and scenery are well-painted. The characters, especially the two police officers, are brought to life well thanks to sufficient background information on their 'makings' as police men.<br /><br />The one disappointment is that - although it might be my own mistake - there seems something quite unlogical about the final revelations of the plot.<br /><br />However, I will most certainly pick up other books by this man.</span>

  <span id="freeText14701218780232516354" style="display:none">Crimson rivers, Grang√©.<br /><br />I need to talk about the cringy writing. The main character (Karim) is terribly portrayed and his insight is a huge caricature. I could see the writer used expressions that sounded, according to him, relavant to a Muslim man. Except that didn‚Äôt work out at all. It was grotesque, and even laughable. I did not, even once, believe in the character‚Äôs reality. <br /><br />However, I must point out that the way the plot is driven is quite interesting. Two main investigators are following two different mysteries, and that makes you wonder ‚Äúhow the hell could that be related?‚Äù And it kept the wonder going, until you piece out the whole picture. <br /><br />Speaking about plot twists, I am disappointed to say that I wasn‚Äôt impressed 70% of the time. And those patronymes were awfully childish. <br /><br />Last but not least. The women. Oh my god. There are a few female characters. And hear me out, they all, without exception, are defined as ‚Äúbeautiful and somewhat seductive‚Äù. Ughh. Even a woman they see once. Or have heard about. They don‚Äôt have any other function! And that annoyed me. Very much. It didn‚Äôt bring anything to the story. <br /><br />I overall were intrigued by the direction his story went, and I hope he got better, because the suspense, at times, was enjoyable. </span>

<div id="review_1164027243" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1164027243" />
    <a title="Ann" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3119697-ann"><img alt="Ann" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/f_50x66-6a03a5c12233c941481992b82eea8d23.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1164027243?book_show_action=true">Jan 10, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ann" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ann" href="/user/show/3119697-ann">Ann</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Mass Market Paperback " href="/book/show/393812.Les_Rivi_res_pourpres">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3119697-ann?shelf=mystery">mystery</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3119697-ann?shelf=french">french</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1164027243" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18409345768874863263">A high-octane psychological thriller about a devilish plot that spans several generations of a French mountain community.<br/><br/>Two hard-boiled French police officers, hundreds of kilometers away from each other, are called in to investigate two separate, but mystifying crimes. Pierre Ni√©mans, a veteran officer, recently in trouble after having dealt too harshly with a football hooligan, is asked to investigate the gruesome murder of R√©my Caillois, a 25-year old librarian in the university town of Guer</span>
  <span id="freeText18409345768874863263" style="display:none">A high-octane psychological thriller about a devilish plot that spans several generations of a French mountain community.<br /><br />Two hard-boiled French police officers, hundreds of kilometers away from each other, are called in to investigate two separate, but mystifying crimes. Pierre Ni√©mans, a veteran officer, recently in trouble after having dealt too harshly with a football hooligan, is asked to investigate the gruesome murder of R√©my Caillois, a 25-year old librarian in the university town of Guernon. Karim Abdouf, a young man of North African origin who became a cop after a hard life amongst the criminals, addicts and prostitutes of Paris, is asked to investigate a seemingly aimless break-in into a school and a minor desecration of a cemetary. Inexorably, over the space of a few days, these 2 independent investigations move towards each other, until they merge. A second victim is found, then a third. There is a link between the fact that all the people involved are 25 years old ‚Äì which would be the age of the child whose grave was searched- and the fact that there are so many children with eye problems in Guernon. <br />The two cops race against the clock, driving from cemeteries to hospitals, from monasteries to university libraries. Soon they discover that the motive for the murders is revenge‚Ä¶ but revenge for what, exactly? The explanation seems to lie in events that happened a generation ago, and which have been covered up with consummate care.<br /><br />The two cops are unusually hard-boiled for French mystery fiction, and their psychology is not particularly well explored. For instance, Pierre Ni√©mans has a dog phobia that is never explained. Both cops seem to function on the principle of ‚ÄúDown these mean streets a man must go‚Äù, and their psychological isolation almost becomes a clich√©. The secondary characters are not memorable, and some of them, like the principal of the school where the break-in occurred, don‚Äôt even seem to be endowed with names. The amount of information that the two cops manage to obtain in their frenetic investigational pace is almost unbelievable. The scientific explanation behind the original conspiracy that unleashed this terrifying vengeance, when it finally emerges, is not particularly sound and seems to have come out of a high school biology textbook. Pierre Ni√©mans was wounded several times in the story, yet kept on going like the energizer bunny. A young man was rejected for his military service on the grounds of acute schizophrenia, and yet no one in the university where he worked had noticed this?! And yet, although I am able to poke holes in individual aspects of the story, it worked for me overall. Perhaps it was the fast pace of the investigation, with new clues being unraveled all the time. Perhaps it was the sheer bizarreness of some of the events (a nun going around begging class pictures off unsuspecting school children? A colony of rats with the names of Guernon families? Acid rain from the 1960s being found in the empty eye sockets of a 1997 corpse?) that kept me riveted to the page. <br /><br />Caution : there is a lot of violence of the book. So this book may work for you if you liked ‚ÄúSilence of the Lambs‚Äù or ‚ÄúThe Girl with the Dragon Tattoo‚Äù, but not if you like Miss Marple and Hercule Poirot!<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="18409345768874863263" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <a title="John" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2763719-john"><img alt="John" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1564310959p2/2763719.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/130537491?book_show_action=true">Nov 12, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="John" class="user" itemprop="url" name="John" href="/user/show/2763719-john">John</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9781860466595" href="/book/show/78678.Blood_Red_Rivers">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2763719-john?shelf=thriller">thriller</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2763719-john?shelf=mystery-detective-fiction">mystery-detective-fiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer130537491" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10585176727837708483">A lean, mean, nasty thrill machine of a novel. Two detectives, each criminals in their own right, team up to solve some brutal ritualistic killings at a French university. Very tightly plotted, but the resolution of the mystery is a just bit to hard to swallow for me to rate this the full five stars. This is a grisly story full of unsavory characters, so be prepared for something dark and macabre. I couldn't read this fast enough, and I really loved the author's unique style and raw energy, but </span>
  <span id="freeText10585176727837708483" style="display:none">A lean, mean, nasty thrill machine of a novel. Two detectives, each criminals in their own right, team up to solve some brutal ritualistic killings at a French university. Very tightly plotted, but the resolution of the mystery is a just bit to hard to swallow for me to rate this the full five stars. This is a grisly story full of unsavory characters, so be prepared for something dark and macabre. I couldn't read this fast enough, and I really loved the author's unique style and raw energy, but some things nevertheless seemed just a little bit lost in translation from the original French. The movie is pretty excellent also, but I'd recommend the book as being the better choice. </span>
  <a data-text-id="10585176727837708483" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

              <span id="reviewTextContainer14011862" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12693593434505617709">Gripping thriller. I couldn't stop reading it til I reached last page. Confrontation young inspector with old one - both alienated in places of their work - and their cooperation in trying to solve mysteries of little boy's grave profanation, murders and weird acting of some people in small French towns. Do devils really exist and kill people in places forgotten by God?? Just read the book and find out.</span>

          </span>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('bch1mt1X5vMHrIXfQrVtS7lYj0r+n3BL4jHmW0iO3zbo5Z+aNpPH1+Sfcbf2zwP3iR3xgPkghwZMIQth46JeOA==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('57qFkF0tSNks0nWOx4dWWJ34KVXAk7Ei2319Ga5aPcpil2+Qtulp/c/hgeZz/Tjkrb1Xn8csRm91bZAjBXa8xA==')})
  }

This partial loads on almost every page view.  The associated React component makes
a call to SignInPromptController#get to determine if the user should see the sign in interstial.
This is determined by how many signed out pagehits the user has executed an how recently they have
last seen the insterstitial.  If the controller responds indicating the popup should appear, the
